## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of concentration change dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem of chemical kinetics rate law determination. The rate typically follows power-law dependence on concentration, with possible time-dependent modulation.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration, radioactive decay, unimolecular reactions)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + A)**(-1) (enzyme kinetics, saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (product-catalyzed reaction)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A)**(-2) (surface-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Time-modulated first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Parallel pathway with time: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t (combined kinetic and time-dependent source term)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order kinetics with constant source/sink)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + A**2)**(-1) (substrate inhibition)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 + A**c1)**(-1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration power-law dependence → dA/dt ~ A^n indicates the molecularity or effective reaction order n of the rate-determining step
- Negative rate constant sign → c0 < 0 indicates consumption/decay of species A rather than production
- Rational function of concentration → saturation behavior indicates enzyme catalysis or surface adsorption limiting the rate
- Constant additive term in rate law → indicates a zero-order source or sink (e.g., constant feed, photolysis at fixed intensity)
- Product of A and (1-A/c) terms → logistic-like kinetics indicating approach to equilibrium or carrying capacity in autocatalysis
- Explicit time dependence multiplying concentration terms → suggests time-varying external conditions (temperature program, light intensity changes)
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → competing parallel reaction pathways with different orders
- Denominator polynomial in A → inhibition or saturation effects from Langmuir-type adsorption or enzyme kinetics mechanisms
- Square root of concentration (A**0.5) → half-order kinetics typical of chain reactions or diffusion-limited surface reactions

$$-0.15727681835797813 \cdot A + 0.49113636468363491 \cdot \sin(\log(A + 1))$$

This has the form: `c0*A + c1*sin(log(A + c2))` where the `_t` variable is absorbed into `c1` (since `_t` is a fixed constant = 3.122751145472426).

- `c0 = -0.15727681835797813`
- `c2 = 1` (so the argument of log is not scaled)
- `c3 = 1` (so `A*c3 + 1 = A + 1`)

This exactly matches the GT.
